<pr_description>
[BUG]: File Parsing Fails for URLs Without Explicit File Extensions
### How are you running AnythingLLM?

All versions

### What happened?

When attempting to pull and parse a file using either the RAG Modal or `@agent` mode, the process fails if the URL does not explicitly end with a file extension (e.g., `.pdf`, `.csv`). This occurs even when the server responds with a correct `Content-Type` header that identifies the file type.

**Example:**

The following URL fails to be processed, despite responding with an `application/pdf` content type:

https://arxiv.org/pdf/2307.10265

**Observed Behavior:**

The application logs display the following error:

```

[2] Error processing single file File extension .10265 not supported for parsing and cannot be assumed as text file type.

```

This error originates from the file extension guard located at:

https://github.com/Mintplex-Labs/anything-llm/blob/89a01492b51a23150b59732166b90ebdd1843c50/collector/processSingleFile/index.js#L58-L72

**Expected Behavior:**

The system should be able to successfully pull and parse files from URLs that do not explicitly contain a file extension, provided the `Content-Type` header in the server's response clearly indicates the file's MIME type.

---

### Are there known steps to reproduce?

_No response_

</pr_description>

     1	const path = require("path");
     2	const fs = require("fs");
     3	const {
     4	  WATCH_DIRECTORY,
     5	  SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS,
     6	} = require("../utils/constants");
     7	const {
     8	  trashFile,
     9	  isTextType,
    10	  normalizePath,
    11	  isWithin,
    12	} = require("../utils/files");
    13	const RESERVED_FILES = ["__HOTDIR__.md"];
    14	
    15	/**
    16	 * Process a single file and return the documents
    17	 * @param {string} targetFilename - The filename to process
    18	 * @param {Object} options - The options for the file processing
    19	 * @param {boolean} options.parseOnly - If true, the file will not be saved as a document even when `writeToServerDocuments` is called in the handler. Must be explicitly set to true to use.
    20	 * @param {Object} metadata - The metadata for the file processing
    21	 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, reason: string, documents: Object[]}>} - The documents from the file processing
    22	 */
    23	async function processSingleFile(targetFilename, options = {}, metadata = {}) {
    24	  const fullFilePath = path.resolve(
    25	    WATCH_DIRECTORY,
    26	    normalizePath(targetFilename)
    27	  );
    28	  if (!isWithin(path.resolve(WATCH_DIRECTORY), fullFilePath))
    29	    return {
    30	      success: false,
    31	      reason: "Filename is a not a valid path to process.",
    32	      documents: [],
    33	    };
    34	
    35	  if (RESERVED_FILES.includes(targetFilename))
    36	    return {
    37	      success: false,
    38	      reason: "Filename is a reserved filename and cannot be processed.",
    39	      documents: [],
    40	    };
    41	  if (!fs.existsSync(fullFilePath))
    42	    return {
    43	      success: false,
    44	      reason: "File does not exist in upload directory.",
    45	      documents: [],
    46	    };
    47	
    48	  const fileExtension = path.extname(fullFilePath).toLowerCase();
    49	  if (fullFilePath.includes(".") && !fileExtension) {
    50	    return {
    51	      success: false,
    52	      reason: `No file extension found. This file cannot be processed.`,
    53	      documents: [],
    54	    };
    55	  }
    56	
    57	  let processFileAs = fileExtension;
    58	  if (!SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS.hasOwnProperty(fileExtension)) {
    59	    if (isTextType(fullFilePath)) {
    60	      console.log(
    61	        `\x1b[33m[Collector]\x1b[0m The provided filetype of ${fileExtension} does not have a preset and will be processed as .txt.`
    62	      );
    63	      processFileAs = ".txt";
    64	    } else {
    65	      trashFile(fullFilePath);
    66	      return {
    67	        success: false,
    68	        reason: `File extension ${fileExtension} not supported for parsing and cannot be assumed as text file type.`,
    69	        documents: [],
    70	      };
    71	    }
    72	  }
    73	
    74	  const FileTypeProcessor = require(SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS[
    75	    processFileAs
    76	  ]);
    77	  return await FileTypeProcessor({
    78	    fullFilePath,
    79	    filename: targetFilename,
    80	    options,
    81	    metadata,
    82	  });
    83	}
    84	
    85	module.exports = {
    86	  processSingleFile,
    87	};
    88

     1	const { validURL } = require("../utils/url");
     2	const { scrapeGenericUrl } = require("./convert/generic");
     3	const { validateURL } = require("../utils/url");
     4	
     5	/**
     6	 * Process a link and return the text content. This util will save the link as a document
     7	 * so it can be used for embedding later.
     8	 * @param {string} link - The link to process
     9	 * @param {{[key: string]: string}} scraperHeaders - Custom headers to apply when scraping the link
    10	 * @param {Object} metadata - Optional metadata to attach to the document
    11	 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, content: string}>} - Response from collector
    12	 */
    13	async function processLink(link, scraperHeaders = {}, metadata = {}) {
    14	  const validatedLink = validateURL(link);
    15	  if (!validURL(validatedLink))
    16	    return { success: false, reason: "Not a valid URL." };
    17	  return await scrapeGenericUrl({
    18	    link: validatedLink,
    19	    captureAs: "text",
    20	    scraperHeaders,
    21	    metadata,
    22	    saveAsDocument: true,
    23	  });
    24	}
    25	
    26	/**
    27	 * Get the text content of a link - does not save the link as a document
    28	 * Mostly used in agentic flows/tools calls to get the text content of a link
    29	 * @param {string} link - The link to get the text content of
    30	 * @param {('html' | 'text' | 'json')} captureAs - The format to capture the page content as
    31	 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, content: string}>} - Response from collector
    32	 */
    33	async function getLinkText(link, captureAs = "text") {
    34	  const validatedLink = validateURL(link);
    35	  if (!validURL(validatedLink))
    36	    return { success: false, reason: "Not a valid URL." };
    37	  return await scrapeGenericUrl({
    38	    link: validatedLink,
    39	    captureAs,
    40	    saveAsDocument: false,
    41	  });
    42	}
    43	
    44	module.exports = {
    45	  processLink,
    46	  getLinkText,
    47	};

     1	const { v4 } = require("uuid");
     2	const {
     3	  PuppeteerWebBaseLoader,
     4	} = require("langchain/document_loaders/web/puppeteer");
     5	const { writeToServerDocuments } = require("../../utils/files");
     6	const { tokenizeString } = require("../../utils/tokenizer");
     7	const { default: slugify } = require("slugify");
     8	const {
     9	  returnResult,
    10	  determineContentType,
    11	  processAsFile,
    12	} = require("../helpers");
    13	const {
    14	  loadYouTubeTranscript,
    15	} = require("../../utils/extensions/YoutubeTranscript");
    16	const RuntimeSettings = require("../../utils/runtimeSettings");
    17	
    18	/**
    19	 * Scrape a generic URL and return the content in the specified format
    20	 * @param {Object} config - The configuration object
    21	 * @param {string} config.link - The URL to scrape
    22	 * @param {('html' | 'text')} config.captureAs - The format to capture the page content as. Default is 'text'
    23	 * @param {{[key: string]: string}} config.scraperHeaders - Custom headers to use when making the request
    24	 * @param {{[key: string]: string}} config.metadata - Metadata to use when creating the document
    25	 * @param {boolean} config.saveAsDocument - Whether to save the content as a document. Default is true
    26	 * @returns {Promise<Object>} - The content of the page
    27	 */
    28	async function scrapeGenericUrl({
    29	  link,
    30	  captureAs = "text",
    31	  scraperHeaders = {},
    32	  metadata = {},
    33	  saveAsDocument = true,
    34	}) {
    35	  /** @type {'web' | 'file' | 'youtube'} */
    36	  console.log(`-- Working URL ${link} => (captureAs: ${captureAs}) --`);
    37	  let { contentType, processVia } = await determineContentType(link);
    38	  console.log(`-- URL determined to be ${contentType} (${processVia}) --`);
    39	
    40	  /**
    41	   * When the content is a file or a YouTube video, we can use the existing processing functions
    42	   * These are self-contained and will return the correct response based on the saveAsDocument flag already
    43	   * so we can return the content immediately.
    44	   */
    45	  if (processVia === "file")
    46	    return await processAsFile({ uri: link, saveAsDocument });
    47	  else if (processVia === "youtube")
    48	    return await loadYouTubeTranscript(
    49	      { url: link },
    50	      { parseOnly: saveAsDocument === false }
    51	    );
    52	
    53	  // Otherwise, assume the content is a webpage and scrape the content from the webpage
    54	  const content = await getPageContent({
    55	    link,
    56	    captureAs,
    57	    headers: scraperHeaders,
    58	  });
    59	  if (!content || !content.length) {
    60	    console.error(`Resulting URL content was empty at ${link}.`);
    61	    return returnResult({
    62	      success: false,
    63	      reason: `No URL content found at ${link}.`,
    64	      documents: [],
    65	      content: null,
    66	      saveAsDocument,
    67	    });
    68	  }
    69	
    70	  // If the captureAs is text, return the content as a string immediately
    71	  // so that we dont save the content as a document
    72	  if (!saveAsDocument)
    73	    return returnResult({
    74	      success: true,
    75	      content,
    76	      saveAsDocument,
    77	    });
    78	
    79	  // Save the content as a document from the URL
    80	  const url = new URL(link);
    81	  const decodedPathname = decodeURIComponent(url.pathname);
    82	  const filename = `${url.hostname}${decodedPathname.replace(/\//g, "_")}`;
    83	  const data = {
    84	    id: v4(),
    85	    url: "file://" + slugify(filename) + ".html",
    86	    title: metadata.title || slugify(filename) + ".html",
    87	    docAuthor: metadata.docAuthor || "no author found",
    88	    description: metadata.description || "No description found.",
    89	    docSource: metadata.docSource || "URL link uploaded by the user.",
    90	    chunkSource: `link://${link}`,
    91	    published: new Date().toLocaleString(),
    92	    wordCount: content.split(" ").length,
    93	    pageContent: content,
    94	    token_count_estimate: tokenizeString(content),
    95	  };
    96	
    97	  const document = writeToServerDocuments({
    98	    data,
    99	    filename: `url-${slugify(filename)}-${data.id}`,
   100	  });
   101	  console.log(`[SUCCESS]: URL ${link} converted & ready for embedding.\n`);
   102	  return { success: true, reason: null, documents: [document] };
   103	}
   104	
   105	/**
   106	 * Validate the headers object
   107	 * - Keys & Values must be strings and not empty
   108	 * - Assemble a new object with only the valid keys and values
   109	 * @param {{[key: string]: string}} headers - The headers object to validate
   110	 * @returns {{[key: string]: string}} - The validated headers object
   111	 */
   112	function validatedHeaders(headers = {}) {
   113	  try {
   114	    if (Object.keys(headers).length === 0) return {};
   115	    let validHeaders = {};
   116	    for (const key of Object.keys(headers)) {
   117	      if (!key?.trim()) continue;
   118	      if (typeof headers[key] !== "string" || !headers[key]?.trim()) continue;
   119	      validHeaders[key] = headers[key].trim();
   120	    }
   121	    return validHeaders;
   122	  } catch (error) {
   123	    console.error("Error validating headers", error);
   124	    return {};
   125	  }
   126	}
   127	
   128	/**
   129	 * Get the content of a page
   130	 * @param {Object} config - The configuration object
   131	 * @param {string} config.link - The URL to get the content of
   132	 * @param {('html' | 'text')} config.captureAs - The format to capture the page content as. Default is 'text'
   133	 * @param {{[key: string]: string}} config.headers - Custom headers to use when making the request
   134	 * @returns {Promise<string>} - The content of the page
   135	 */
   136	async function getPageContent({ link, captureAs = "text", headers = {} }) {
   137	  try {
   138	    let pageContents = [];
   139	    const runtimeSettings = new RuntimeSettings();
   140	
   141	    /** @type {import('puppeteer').PuppeteerLaunchOptions} */
   142	    let launchConfig = { headless: "new" };
   143	
   144	    /* On MacOS 15.1, the headless=new option causes the browser to crash immediately.
   145	     * It is not clear why this is the case, but it is reproducible. Since AnythinglLM
   146	     * in production runs in a container, we can disable headless mode to workaround the issue for development purposes.
   147	     *
   148	     * This may show a popup window when scraping a page in development mode.
   149	     * This is expected behavior if seen in development mode on MacOS 15+
   150	     */
   151	    if (
   152	      process.platform === "darwin" &&
   153	      process.env.NODE_ENV === "development"
   154	    ) {
   155	      console.log(
   156	        "Darwin Development Mode: Disabling headless mode to prevent Chromium from crashing."
   157	      );
   158	      launchConfig.headless = "false";
   159	    }
   160	
   161	    const loader = new PuppeteerWebBaseLoader(link, {
   162	      launchOptions: {
   163	        headless: launchConfig.headless,
   164	        ignoreHTTPSErrors: true,
   165	        args: runtimeSettings.get("browserLaunchArgs"),
   166	      },
   167	      gotoOptions: {
   168	        waitUntil: "networkidle2",
   169	      },
   170	      async evaluate(page, browser) {
   171	        const result = await page.evaluate((captureAs) => {
   172	          if (captureAs === "text") return document.body.innerText;
   173	          if (captureAs === "html") return document.documentElement.innerHTML;
   174	          return document.body.innerText;
   175	        }, captureAs);
   176	        await browser.close();
   177	        return result;
   178	      },
   179	    });
   180	
   181	    // Override scrape method if headers are available
   182	    let overrideHeaders = validatedHeaders(headers);
   183	    if (Object.keys(overrideHeaders).length > 0) {
   184	      loader.scrape = async function () {
   185	        const { launch } = await PuppeteerWebBaseLoader.imports();
   186	        const browser = await launch({
   187	          headless: "new",
   188	          defaultViewport: null,
   189	          ignoreDefaultArgs: ["--disable-extensions"],
   190	          ...this.options?.launchOptions,
   191	        });
   192	        const page = await browser.newPage();
   193	        await page.setExtraHTTPHeaders(overrideHeaders);
   194	
   195	        await page.goto(this.webPath, {
   196	          timeout: 180000,
   197	          waitUntil: "networkidle2",
   198	          ...this.options?.gotoOptions,
   199	        });
   200	
   201	        const bodyHTML = this.options?.evaluate
   202	          ? await this.options.evaluate(page, browser)
   203	          : await page.evaluate(() => document.body.innerHTML);
   204	
   205	        await browser.close();
   206	        return bodyHTML;
   207	      };
   208	    }
   209	
   210	    const docs = await loader.load();
   211	    for (const doc of docs) pageContents.push(doc.pageContent);
   212	    return pageContents.join(" ");
   213	  } catch (error) {
   214	    console.error(
   215	      "getPageContent failed to be fetched by puppeteer - falling back to fetch!",
   216	      error
   217	    );
   218	  }
   219	
   220	  try {
   221	    const pageText = await fetch(link, {
   222	      method: "GET",
   223	      headers: {
   224	        "Content-Type": "text/plain",
   225	        "User-Agent":
   226	          "Mozilla/5.0 (Macintosh; Intel Mac OS X 10_15_4) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/85.0.4183.83 Safari/537.36,gzip(gfe)",
   227	        ...validatedHeaders(headers),
   228	      },
   229	    }).then((res) => res.text());
   230	    return pageText;
   231	  } catch (error) {
   232	    console.error("getPageContent failed to be fetched by any method.", error);
   233	  }
   234	
   235	  return null;
   236	}
   237	
   238	module.exports = {
   239	  scrapeGenericUrl,
   240	};
   241

     1	const path = require("path");
     2	const { validURL } = require("../../utils/url");
     3	const { processSingleFile } = require("../../processSingleFile");
     4	const { downloadURIToFile } = require("../../utils/downloadURIToFile");
     5	const { ACCEPTED_MIMES } = require("../../utils/constants");
     6	const { validYoutubeVideoUrl } = require("../../utils/url");
     7	
     8	/**
     9	 * Get the content type of a resource
    10	 * - Sends a HEAD request to the URL and returns the Content-Type header with a 5 second timeout
    11	 * @param {string} url - The URL to get the content type of
    12	 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, reason: string|null, contentType: string|null}>} - The content type of the resource
    13	 */
    14	async function getContentTypeFromURL(url) {
    15	  try {
    16	    if (!url || typeof url !== "string" || !validURL(url))
    17	      return { success: false, reason: "Not a valid URL.", contentType: null };
    18	
    19	    const abortController = new AbortController();
    20	    const timeout = setTimeout(() => {
    21	      abortController.abort();
    22	      console.error("Timeout fetching content type for URL:", url.toString());
    23	    }, 5_000);
    24	
    25	    const res = await fetch(url, {
    26	      method: "HEAD",
    27	      signal: abortController.signal,
    28	    }).finally(() => clearTimeout(timeout));
    29	
    30	    if (!res.ok)
    31	      return {
    32	        success: false,
    33	        reason: `HTTP ${res.status}: ${res.statusText}`,
    34	        contentType: null,
    35	      };
    36	
    37	    const contentType = res.headers.get("Content-Type")?.toLowerCase();
    38	    const contentTypeWithoutCharset = contentType?.split(";")[0].trim();
    39	    if (!contentTypeWithoutCharset)
    40	      return {
    41	        success: false,
    42	        reason: "No Content-Type found.",
    43	        contentType: null,
    44	      };
    45	    return {
    46	      success: true,
    47	      reason: null,
    48	      contentType: contentTypeWithoutCharset,
    49	    };
    50	  } catch (error) {
    51	    return {
    52	      success: false,
    53	      reason: `Error: ${error.message}`,
    54	      contentType: null,
    55	    };
    56	  }
    57	}
    58	
    59	/**
    60	 * Normalize the result object based on the saveAsDocument flag
    61	 * @param {Object} result - The result object to normalize
    62	 * @param {boolean} result.success - Whether the result is successful
    63	 * @param {string|null} result.reason - The reason for the result
    64	 * @param {Object[]} result.documents - The documents from the result
    65	 * @param {string|null} result.content - The content of the result
    66	 * @param {boolean} result.saveAsDocument - Whether to save the content as a document. Default is true
    67	 * @returns {{success: boolean, reason: string|null, documents: Object[], content: string|null}} - The normalized result object
    68	 */
    69	function returnResult({
    70	  success,
    71	  reason,
    72	  documents,
    73	  content,
    74	  saveAsDocument = true,
    75	} = {}) {
    76	  if (!saveAsDocument) {
    77	    return {
    78	      success,
    79	      content,
    80	    };
    81	  } else return { success, reason, documents };
    82	}
    83	
    84	/**
    85	 * Determine the content type of a link - should be a URL
    86	 * @param {string} uri - The link to determine the content type of
    87	 * @returns {Promise<{contentType: string|null, processVia: 'web' | 'file' | 'youtube'}>} - The content type of the link
    88	 */
    89	async function determineContentType(uri) {
    90	  let processVia = "web";
    91	
    92	  // Dont check for content type if it is a YouTube video URL
    93	  if (validYoutubeVideoUrl(uri))
    94	    return { contentType: "text/html", processVia: "youtube" };
    95	
    96	  return await getContentTypeFromURL(uri)
    97	    .then((result) => {
    98	      if (!!result.reason) console.error(result.reason);
    99	
   100	      // If the content type is not text/html or text/plain, and it is in the ACCEPTED_MIMES,
   101	      // then we can process it as a file
   102	      if (
   103	        !!result.contentType &&
   104	        !["text/html", "text/plain"].includes(result.contentType) &&
   105	        result.contentType in ACCEPTED_MIMES
   106	      )
   107	        processVia = "file";
   108	
   109	      return { contentType: result.contentType, processVia };
   110	    })
   111	    .catch((error) => {
   112	      console.error("Error getting content type from URL", error);
   113	      return { contentType: null, processVia };
   114	    });
   115	}
   116	
   117	/**
   118	 * Process a link as a file
   119	 * @param {string} uri - The link to process as a file
   120	 * @param {boolean} saveAsDocument - Whether to save the content as a document. Default is true
   121	 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, reason: string|null, documents: Object[], content: string|null, saveAsDocument: boolean}>} - The content of the file
   122	 */
   123	async function processAsFile({ uri, saveAsDocument = true }) {
   124	  const fileContentResult = await downloadURIToFile(uri);
   125	  if (!fileContentResult.success)
   126	    return returnResult({
   127	      success: false,
   128	      reason: fileContentResult.reason,
   129	      documents: [],
   130	      content: null,
   131	      saveAsDocument,
   132	    });
   133	
   134	  const fileFilePath = fileContentResult.fileLocation;
   135	  const targetFilename = path.basename(fileFilePath);
   136	
   137	  /**
   138	   * If the saveAsDocument is false, we are only interested in the text content
   139	   * and can ignore the file as a document by using `parseOnly` in the options.
   140	   * This will send the file to the Direct Uploads folder instead of the Documents folder.
   141	   * that will be deleted by the cleanup-orphan-documents job that runs frequently. The trade off
   142	   * is that since it still is in FS we can debug its output or even potentially reuse it for other purposes.
   143	   *
   144	   * TODO: Improve this process via a new option that will instantly delete the file after processing
   145	   * if we find we dont need this file ever after processing.
   146	   */
   147	  const processSingleFileResult = await processSingleFile(targetFilename, {
   148	    parseOnly: saveAsDocument === false,
   149	  });
   150	  if (!processSingleFileResult.success) {
   151	    return returnResult({
   152	      success: false,
   153	      reason: processSingleFileResult.reason,
   154	      documents: [],
   155	      content: null,
   156	      saveAsDocument,
   157	    });
   158	  }
   159	
   160	  // If we intend to return only the text content, return the content from the file
   161	  // and then delete the file - otherwise it will be saved as a document
   162	  if (!saveAsDocument) {
   163	    return returnResult({
   164	      success: true,
   165	      content: processSingleFileResult.documents[0].pageContent,
   166	      saveAsDocument,
   167	    });
   168	  }
   169	
   170	  return processSingleFileResult;
   171	}
   172	
   173	module.exports = {
   174	  returnResult,
   175	  getContentTypeFromURL,
   176	  determineContentType,
   177	  processAsFile,
   178	};

Here's the result of running `cat -n` on /testbed/collector/utils/downloadURIToFile/index.js:
     1	const { WATCH_DIRECTORY } = require("../constants");
     2	const fs = require("fs");
     3	const path = require("path");
     4	const { pipeline } = require("stream/promises");
     5	const { validURL } = require("../url");
     6	const { default: slugify } = require("slugify");
     7	
     8	/**
     9	 * Download a file to the hotdir
    10	 * @param {string} url - The URL of the file to download
    11	 * @param {number} maxTimeout - The maximum timeout in milliseconds
    12	 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, fileLocation: string|null, reason: string|null}>} - The path to the downloaded file
    13	 */
    14	async function downloadURIToFile(url, maxTimeout = 10_000) {
    15	  if (!url || typeof url !== "string" || !validURL(url))
    16	    return { success: false, reason: "Not a valid URL.", fileLocation: null };
    17	
    18	  try {
    19	    const abortController = new AbortController();
    20	    const timeout = setTimeout(() => {
    21	      abortController.abort();
    22	      console.error(
    23	        `Timeout ${maxTimeout}ms reached while downloading file for URL:`,
    24	        url.toString()
    25	      );
    26	    }, maxTimeout);
    27	
    28	    const res = await fetch(url, { signal: abortController.signal })
    29	      .then((res) => {
    30	        if (!res.ok) throw new Error(`HTTP ${res.status}: ${res.statusText}`);
    31	        return res;
    32	      })
    33	      .finally(() => clearTimeout(timeout));
    34	
    35	    const urlObj = new URL(url);
    36	    const filename = `${urlObj.hostname}-${slugify(
    37	      urlObj.pathname.replace(/\//g, "-"),
    38	      { lower: true }
    39	    )}`;
    40	    const localFilePath = path.join(WATCH_DIRECTORY, filename);
    41	    const writeStream = fs.createWriteStream(localFilePath);
    42	    await pipeline(res.body, writeStream);
    43	
    44	    console.log(`[SUCCESS]: File ${localFilePath} downloaded to hotdir.`);
    45	    return { success: true, fileLocation: localFilePath, reason: null };
    46	  } catch (error) {
    47	    console.error(`Error writing to hotdir: ${error} for URL: ${url}`);
    48	    return { success: false, reason: error.message, fileLocation: null };
    49	  }
    50	}
    51	
    52	module.exports = {
    53	  downloadURIToFile,
    54	};
    55

2026-05-30 06:47:33,065 - INFO - swea-agent-Mintplex-Labs__anything-llm-5252 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I have a clear picture. Let me trace the flow:

1. When a URL like `https://arxiv.org/pdf/2307.10265` is processed, `determineContentType` in `helpers/index.js` sends a HEAD request to get the Content-Type.
2. If the Content-Type is `application/pdf` (which is in `ACCEPTED_MIMES`), `processVia` is set to `"file"`.
3. The flow goes to `processAsFile`, which calls `downloadURIToFile` to download the file.
4. `downloadURIToFile` saves the file with a filename derived from the URL path: `arxiv.org-pdf-2307.10265` (since pathname is `/pdf/2307.10265`).
5. Then `processSingleFile` is called on that filename. In `processSingleFile`, `path.extname(fullFilePath)` returns `.10265` (since the filename is `arxiv.org-pdf-2307.10265` and the last dot-separated segment is `10265`).
6. Since `.10265` is not in `SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS` and it's not a text type, it fails with "File extension .10265 not supported..."

The problem is in multiple places:

1. **`downloadURIToFile`**: When saving the file, it should preserve or infer the correct file extension from the Content-Type header, rather than just using the URL pathname.

2. **`processSingleFile`**: The extension checking logic could also be improved to handle cases where the extension is not known but the file type could be inferred.

The most appropriate fix is in `downloadURIToFile`: when downloading a file, we should also get the Content-Type from the response and append the appropriate file extension based on `ACCEPTED_MIMES` mapping.

But wait, let me also check: the `processSingleFile` function could also be improved. Let's look at where the error message from the PR description comes from:

The PR says the error is at `processSingleFile/index.js#L58-L72` which is exactly:
```js
if (!SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS.hasOwnProperty(fileExtension)) {
    if (isTextType(fullFilePath)) {
      // ...process as .txt
    } else {
      trashFile(fullFilePath);
      return {
        success: false,
        reason: `File extension ${fileExtension} not supported for parsing and cannot be assumed as text file type.`,
      };
    }
  }
```

So there are two approaches:
1. Fix `downloadURIToFile` to append the correct extension from Content-Type
2. Fix `processSingleFile` to be more resilient when extension is unknown

The best approach is to fix `downloadURIToFile` to use the Content-Type to determine the proper file extension. Let me also check the `files` utility:

    24	/**
    25	 * Checks if a file is text by checking the mime type and then falling back to buffer inspection.
    26	 * This way we can capture all the cases where the mime type is not known but still parseable as text
    27	 * without having to constantly add new mime type overrides.
    28	 * @param {string} filepath - The path to the file.
    29	 * @returns {boolean} - Returns true if the file is text, false otherwise.
    30	 */
    31	function isTextType(filepath) {
    32	  if (!fs.existsSync(filepath)) return false;
    33	  const result = isKnownTextMime(filepath);
    34	  if (result.valid) return true; // Known text type - return true.
    35	  if (result.reason !== "generic") return false; // If any other reason than generic - return false.
    36	  return parseableAsText(filepath); // Fallback to parsing as text via buffer inspection.
    37	}
    38	
    39	/**
    40	 * Checks if a file is known to be text by checking the mime type.
    41	 * @param {string} filepath - The path to the file.
    42	 * @returns {boolean} - Returns true if the file is known to be text, false otherwise.
    43	 */
    44	function isKnownTextMime(filepath) {
    45	  try {
    46	    const mimeLib = new MimeDetector();
    47	    const mime = mimeLib.getType(filepath);
    48	    if (mimeLib.badMimes.includes(mime))
    49	      return { valid: false, reason: "bad_mime" };
    50	
    51	    const type = mime.split("/")[0];
    52	    if (mimeLib.nonTextTypes.includes(type))
    53	      return { valid: false, reason: "non_text_mime" };
    54	    return { valid: true, reason: "valid_mime" };
    55	  } catch {
    56	    return { valid: false, reason: "generic" };
    57	  }
    58	}
    59	
    60	/**
    61	 * Checks if a file is parseable as text by forcing it to be read as text in utf8 encoding.
    62	 * If the file looks too much like a binary file, it will return false.
    63	 * @param {string} filepath - The path to the file.
    64	 * @returns {boolean} - Returns true if the file is parseable as text, false otherwise.
    65	 */
    66	function parseableAsText(filepath) {
    67	  try {
    68	    const fd = fs.openSync(filepath, "r");
    69	    const buffer = Buffer.alloc(1024); // Read first 1KB of the file synchronously
    70	    const bytesRead = fs.readSync(fd, buffer, 0, 1024, 0);
    71	    fs.closeSync(fd);
    72	
    73	    const content = buffer.subarray(0, bytesRead).toString("utf8");
    74	    const nullCount = (content.match(/\0/g) || []).length;
    75	    //eslint-disable-next-line
    76	    const controlCount = (content.match(/[\x00-\x08\x0B\x0C\x0E-\x1F]/g) || [])
    77	      .length;
    78	
    79	    const threshold = bytesRead * 0.1;
    80	    return nullCount + controlCount < threshold;
    81	  } catch {
    82	    return false;
    83	  }
    84	}
    85	
    86	function trashFile(filepath) {
    87	  if (!fs.existsSync(filepath)) return;
    88	
    89	  try {
    90	    const isDir = fs.lstatSync(filepath).isDirectory();
    91	    if (isDir) return;
    92	  } catch {
    93	    return;
    94	  }
    95	
    96	  fs.rmSync(filepath);
    97	  return;
    98	}
    99	
   100	function createdDate(filepath) {
   101	  try {
   102	    const { birthtimeMs, birthtime } = fs.statSync(filepath);
   103	    if (birthtimeMs === 0) throw new Error("Invalid stat for file!");
   104	    return birthtime.toLocaleString();
   105	  } catch {
   106	    return "unknown";
   107	  }
   108	}
   109	
   110	/**
   111	 * Writes a document to the server documents folder.
   112	 * @param {Object} params - The parameters for the function.
   113	 * @param {Object} params.data - The data to write to the file. Must look like a document object.
   114	 * @param {string} params.filename - The name of the file to write to.
   115	 * @param {string|null} params.destinationOverride - A forced destination to write to - will be honored if provided.
   116	 * @param {Object} params.options - The options for the function.
   117	 * @param {boolean} params.options.parseOnly - If true, the file will be written to the direct uploads folder instead of the documents folder. Will be ignored if destinationOverride is provided.
   118	 * @returns {Object} - The data with the location added.
   119	 */
   120	function writeToServerDocuments({
   121	  data = {},
   122	  filename,
   123	  destinationOverride = null,
   124	  options = {},
   125	}) {
   126	  if (!filename) throw new Error("Filename is required!");
   127	
   128	  let destination = null;
   129	  if (destinationOverride) destination = path.resolve(destinationOverride);
   130	  else if (options.parseOnly) destination = path.resolve(directUploadsFolder);
   131	  else destination = path.resolve(documentsFolder, "custom-documents");
   132	
   133	  if (!fs.existsSync(destination))
   134	    fs.mkdirSync(destination, { recursive: true });
   135	  const destinationFilePath = normalizePath(
   136	    path.resolve(destination, filename) + ".json"
   137	  );
   138	
   139	  fs.writeFileSync(destinationFilePath, JSON.stringify(data, null, 4), {
   140	    encoding: "utf-8",
   141	  });
   142	
   143	  return {
   144	    ...data,
   145	    // relative location string that can be passed into the /update-embeddings api
   146	    // that will work since we know the location exists and since we only allow
   147	    // 1-level deep folders this will always work. This still works for integrations like GitHub and YouTube.
   148	    location: destinationFilePath.split("/").slice(-2).join("/"),
   149	    isDirectUpload: options.parseOnly || false,
   150	  };
   151	}

   153	// When required we can wipe the entire collector hotdir and tmp storage in case
   154	// there were some large file failures that we unable to be removed a reboot will
   155	// force remove them.
   156	async function wipeCollectorStorage() {
   157	  const cleanHotDir = new Promise((resolve) => {
   158	    const directory = path.resolve(__dirname, "../../hotdir");
   159	    fs.readdir(directory, (err, files) => {
   160	      if (err) resolve();

   163	        if (file === "__HOTDIR__.md") continue;
   164	        try {

   167	      }

   169	    });
   170	  });

   174	    fs.readdir(directory, (err, files) => {
   175	      if (err) resolve();

   179	        try {

   181	        } catch {}
   182	      }
   183	      resolve();
   184	    });
   185	  });
   186	
   187	  await Promise.all([cleanHotDir, cleanTmpDir]);
   188	  console.log(`Collector hot directory and tmp storage wiped!`);
   189	  return;
   190	}
   191	
   192	/**
   193	 * Checks if a given path is within another path.
   194	 * @param {string} outer - The outer path (should be resolved).
   195	 * @param {string} inner - The inner path (should be resolved).
   196	 * @returns {boolean} - Returns true if the inner path is within the outer path, false otherwise.
   197	 */
   198	function isWithin(outer, inner) {
   199	  if (outer === inner) return false;
   200	  const rel = path.relative(outer, inner);
   201	  return !rel.startsWith("../") && rel !== "..";
   202	}
   203	
   204	function normalizePath(filepath = "") {
   205	  const result = path
   206	    .normalize(filepath.trim())
   207	    .replace(/^(\.\.(\/|\\|$))+/, "")
   208	    .trim();
   209	  if (["..", ".", "/"].includes(result)) throw new Error("Invalid path.");
   210	  return result;
   211	}
   212	
   213	function sanitizeFileName(fileName) {
   214	  if (!fileName) return fileName;
   215	  //eslint-disable-next-line
   216	  return fileName.replace(/[<>:"\/\\|?*]/g, "");
   217	}

- URL: `https://arxiv.org/pdf/2307.10265`
- urlObj.pathname = `/pdf/2307.10265`
- filename = `arxiv.org-pdf-2307.10265` (after slugify and replacing `/` with `-`)
- So the file extension becomes `.10265`

The fix should be in `downloadURIToFile`. We need to:
1. Get the Content-Type from the response headers
2. Use the Content-Type to determine the proper file extension via `ACCEPTED_MIMES`
3. Append the correct extension to the filename

Let me also check if there's a reverse mapping needed (mime type -> extension):

Looking at `ACCEPTED_MIMES`, we have a mapping from MIME type to array of extensions. We need to create a reverse mapping or use the first extension for each MIME type.

This confirms the issue. Now let me implement the fix. The key change should be in `downloadURIToFile` to append the correct extension based on the Content-Type header from the response.

Let me also look at how the file is used after download to make sure we handle everything correctly:

The flow is:
1. `downloadURIToFile(url)` - downloads file, returns `{ success, fileLocation }`
2. `processSingleFile(targetFilename)` - uses `path.extname(fullFilePath)` to get extension and then look up the converter

The fix should be in `downloadURIToFile`: after downloading, we should check the Content-Type header and append the appropriate extension to the filename. Let me also check if we need to handle the case where the Content-Type is not in `ACCEPTED_MIMES`.

But also, looking more at the code, there's another approach: we could fix `processSingleFile` to be more lenient. But the real issue is that the file extension is wrong because of how the filename is constructed in `downloadURIToFile`. The proper fix is to ensure the downloaded file has the correct extension.

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/collector/utils/downloadURIToFile/index.js   --old_str 'const { WATCH_DIRECTORY } = require("../constants");
const fs = require("fs");
const path = require("path");
const { pipeline } = require("stream/promises");
const { validURL } = require("../url");
const { default: slugify } = require("slugify");

/**
 * Download a file to the hotdir
 * @param {string} url - The URL of the file to download
 * @param {number} maxTimeout - The maximum timeout in milliseconds
 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, fileLocation: string|null, reason: string|null}>} - The path to the downloaded file
 */
async function downloadURIToFile(url, maxTimeout = 10_000) {
  if (!url || typeof url !== "string" || !validURL(url))
    return { success: false, reason: "Not a valid URL.", fileLocation: null };

  try {
    const abortController = new AbortController();
    const timeout = setTimeout(() => {
      abortController.abort();
      console.error(
        `Timeout ${maxTimeout}ms reached while downloading file for URL:`,
        url.toString()
      );
    }, maxTimeout);

    const res = await fetch(url, { signal: abortController.signal })
      .then((res) => {
        if (!res.ok) throw new Error(`HTTP ${res.status}: ${res.statusText}`);
        return res;
      })
      .finally(() => clearTimeout(timeout));

    const urlObj = new URL(url);
    const filename = `${urlObj.hostname}-${slugify(
      urlObj.pathname.replace(/\//g, "-"),
      { lower: true }
    )}`;
    const localFilePath = path.join(WATCH_DIRECTORY, filename);
    const writeStream = fs.createWriteStream(localFilePath);
    await pipeline(res.body, writeStream);

    console.log(`[SUCCESS]: File ${localFilePath} downloaded to hotdir.`);
    return { success: true, fileLocation: localFilePath, reason: null };
  } catch (error) {
    console.error(`Error writing to hotdir: ${error} for URL: ${url}`);
    return { success: false, reason: error.message, fileLocation: null };
  }
}' --new_str 'const { WATCH_DIRECTORY, ACCEPTED_MIMES } = require("../constants");
const fs = require("fs");
const path = require("path");
const { pipeline } = require("stream/promises");
const { validURL } = require("../url");
const { default: slugify } = require("slugify");

/**
 * Given a content-type header value, return the best matching file extension.
 * Uses the ACCEPTED_MIMES mapping to find the appropriate extension.
 * If no match is found, returns null.
 * @param {string} contentType - The Content-Type header value
 * @returns {string|null} - The file extension (including the dot) or null
 */
function extensionFromContentType(contentType) {
  if (!contentType) return null;
  // Only take the part before any semicolon (e.g., "application/pdf; charset=utf-8")
  const mimeType = contentType.split(";")[0].trim().toLowerCase();
  if (mimeType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
    // Return the first extension for this MIME type
    return ACCEPTED_MIMES[mimeType][0];
  }
  return null;
}

/**
 * Download a file to the hotdir
 * @param {string} url - The URL of the file to download
 * @param {number} maxTimeout - The maximum timeout in milliseconds
 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, fileLocation: string|null, reason: string|null}>} - The path to the downloaded file
 */
async function downloadURIToFile(url, maxTimeout = 10_000) {
  if (!url || typeof url !== "string" || !validURL(url))
    return { success: false, reason: "Not a valid URL.", fileLocation: null };

  try {
    const abortController = new AbortController();
    const timeout = setTimeout(() => {
      abortController.abort();
      console.error(
        `Timeout ${maxTimeout}ms reached while downloading file for URL:`,
        url.toString()
      );
    }, maxTimeout);

    const res = await fetch(url, { signal: abortController.signal })
      .then((res) => {
        if (!res.ok) throw new Error(`HTTP ${res.status}: ${res.statusText}`);
        return res;
      })
      .finally(() => clearTimeout(timeout));

    const urlObj = new URL(url);
    let filename = `${urlObj.hostname}-${slugify(
      urlObj.pathname.replace(/\//g, "-"),
      { lower: true }
    )}`;

    // Check if the filename already has a valid extension that we support.
    // If not, try to determine the extension from the Content-Type header.
    const currentExt = path.extname(filename).toLowerCase();
    const { SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS } = require("../constants");
    if (!currentExt || !(currentExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
      const contentType = res.headers.get("Content-Type");
      const inferredExt = extensionFromContentType(contentType);
      if (inferredExt) {
        filename = filename + inferredExt;
        console.log(
          `[INFO]: Inferred file extension "${inferredExt}" from Content-Type "${contentType}" for URL: ${url}`
        );
      }
    }

    const localFilePath = path.join(WATCH_DIRECTORY, filename);
    const writeStream = fs.createWriteStream(localFilePath);
    await pipeline(res.body, writeStream);

    console.log(`[SUCCESS]: File ${localFilePath} downloaded to hotdir.`);
    return { success: true, fileLocation: localFilePath, reason: null };
  } catch (error) {
    console.error(`Error writing to hotdir: ${error} for URL: ${url}`);
    return { success: false, reason: error.message, fileLocation: null };
  }
}'

const path = require('path');
const { ACCEPTED_MIMES, SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS } = require('./utils/constants');

function extensionFromContentType(contentType) {
  if (!contentType) return null;
  const mimeType = contentType.split(';')[0].trim().toLowerCase();
  if (mimeType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
    return ACCEPTED_MIMES[mimeType][0];
  }
  return null;
}

// Test 1: arxiv PDF URL
const url = 'https://arxiv.org/pdf/2307.10265';
const urlObj = new URL(url);
const { default: slugify } = require('slugify');
let filename = urlObj.hostname + '-' + slugify(urlObj.pathname.replace(/\//g, '-'), { lower: true });
console.log('Original filename:', filename);
console.log('Original ext:', path.extname(filename));

const contentType = 'application/pdf';
const currentExt = path.extname(filename).toLowerCase();
if (!currentExt || !(currentExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
  const inferredExt = extensionFromContentType(contentType);
  if (inferredExt) {
    filename = filename + inferredExt;
    console.log('New filename:', filename);
    console.log('New ext:', path.extname(filename));
    console.log('Is extension supported?', path.extname(filename).toLowerCase() in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS);
  }
}

console.log('');

// Test 2: URL that already has a proper extension
const url2 = 'https://example.com/document.pdf';
const urlObj2 = new URL(url2);
let filename2 = urlObj2.hostname + '-' + slugify(urlObj2.pathname.replace(/\//g, '-'), { lower: true });
console.log('Test 2 - Original filename:', filename2);
console.log('Test 2 - Original ext:', path.extname(filename2));
console.log('Test 2 - Is extension supported?', path.extname(filename2).toLowerCase() in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS);

console.log('');

// Test 3: URL with CSV content type but no extension
const url3 = 'https://example.com/data/export';
const urlObj3 = new URL(url3);
let filename3 = urlObj3.hostname + '-' + slugify(urlObj3.pathname.replace(/\//g, '-'), { lower: true });
console.log('Test 3 - Original filename:', filename3);
console.log('Test 3 - Original ext:', path.extname(filename3));
const contentType3 = 'text/csv';
const currentExt3 = path.extname(filename3).toLowerCase();
if (!currentExt3 || !(currentExt3 in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
  const inferredExt = extensionFromContentType(contentType3);
  if (inferredExt) {
    filename3 = filename3 + inferredExt;
    console.log('Test 3 - New filename:', filename3);
    console.log('Test 3 - New ext:', path.extname(filename3));
    console.log('Test 3 - Is extension supported?', path.extname(filename3).toLowerCase() in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS);
  }
}

console.log('');

// Test 4: Content-Type with charset
const contentType4 = 'application/pdf; charset=utf-8';
console.log('Test 4 - Content-Type with charset:', contentType4);
console.log('Test 4 - Inferred extension:', extensionFromContentType(contentType4));

console.log('');

// Test 5: Unknown content type
const contentType5 = 'application/octet-stream';
console.log('Test 5 - Unknown content type:', contentType5);
console.log('Test 5 - Inferred extension:', extensionFromContentType(contentType5));

const path = require('path');
const { ACCEPTED_MIMES, SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS } = require('./utils/constants');

function extensionFromContentType(contentType) {
  if (!contentType) return null;
  const mimeType = contentType.split(';')[0].trim().toLowerCase();
  if (mimeType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
    return ACCEPTED_MIMES[mimeType][0];
  }
  return null;
}

// Test 1: arxiv PDF URL
const url = 'https://arxiv.org/pdf/2307.10265';
const urlObj = new URL(url);
const { default: slugify } = require('slugify');
let filename = urlObj.hostname + '-' + slugify(urlObj.pathname.replace(/\//g, '-'), { lower: true });
console.log('Original filename:', filename);
console.log('Original ext:', path.extname(filename));

const contentType = 'application/pdf';
const currentExt = path.extname(filename).toLowerCase();
if (!currentExt || !(currentExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
  const inferredExt = extensionFromContentType(contentType);
  if (inferredExt) {
    filename = filename + inferredExt;
    console.log('New filename:', filename);
    console.log('New ext:', path.extname(filename));
    console.log('Is extension supported?', path.extname(filename).toLowerCase() in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS);
  }
}

console.log('');

// Test 2: URL that already has a proper extension
const url2 = 'https://example.com/document.pdf';
const urlObj2 = new URL(url2);
let filename2 = urlObj2.hostname + '-' + slugify(urlObj2.pathname.replace(/\//g, '-'), { lower: true });
console.log('Test 2 - Original filename:', filename2);
console.log('Test 2 - Original ext:', path.extname(filename2));
console.log('Test 2 - Is extension supported?', path.extname(filename2).toLowerCase() in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS);

console.log('');

// Test 3: URL with CSV content type but no extension
const url3 = 'https://example.com/data/export';
const urlObj3 = new URL(url3);
let filename3 = urlObj3.hostname + '-' + slugify(urlObj3.pathname.replace(/\//g, '-'), { lower: true });
console.log('Test 3 - Original filename:', filename3);
console.log('Test 3 - Original ext:', path.extname(filename3));
const contentType3 = 'text/csv';
const currentExt3 = path.extname(filename3).toLowerCase();
if (!currentExt3 || !(currentExt3 in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
  const inferredExt = extensionFromContentType(contentType3);
  if (inferredExt) {
    filename3 = filename3 + inferredExt;
    console.log('Test 3 - New filename:', filename3);
    console.log('Test 3 - New ext:', path.extname(filename3));
    console.log('Test 3 - Is extension supported?', path.extname(filename3).toLowerCase() in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS);
  }
}

console.log('');

// Test 4: Content-Type with charset
const contentType4 = 'application/pdf; charset=utf-8';
console.log('Test 4 - Content-Type with charset:', contentType4);
console.log('Test 4 - Inferred extension:', extensionFromContentType(contentType4));

console.log('');

// Test 5: Unknown content type
const contentType5 = 'application/octet-stream';
console.log('Test 5 - Unknown content type:', contentType5);
console.log('Test 5 - Inferred extension:', extensionFromContentType(contentType5));

    51	   * Returns the MIME type of the file. If the file has no extension found, it will be processed as a text file.
    52	   * @param {string} filepath
    53	   * @returns {string}
    54	   */
    55	  getType(filepath) {
    56	    const parsedMime = this.lib.getType(filepath);
    57	    if (!!parsedMime) return parsedMime;
    58	    return null;
    59	  }
    60	}
    61

    63	  MimeDetector,
    64	};

     1	const { WATCH_DIRECTORY, ACCEPTED_MIMES } = require("../constants");
     2	const fs = require("fs");
     3	const path = require("path");
     4	const { pipeline } = require("stream/promises");
     5	const { validURL } = require("../url");
     6	const { default: slugify } = require("slugify");
     7	
     8	/**
     9	 * Given a content-type header value, return the best matching file extension.
    10	 * Uses the ACCEPTED_MIMES mapping to find the appropriate extension.
    11	 * If no match is found, returns null.
    12	 * @param {string} contentType - The Content-Type header value
    13	 * @returns {string|null} - The file extension (including the dot) or null
    14	 */
    15	function extensionFromContentType(contentType) {
    16	  if (!contentType) return null;
    17	  // Only take the part before any semicolon (e.g., "application/pdf; charset=utf-8")
    18	  const mimeType = contentType.split(";")[0].trim().toLowerCase();
    19	  if (mimeType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
    20	    // Return the first extension for this MIME type
    21	    return ACCEPTED_MIMES[mimeType][0];
    22	  }
    23	  return null;
    24	}
    25	
    26	/**
    27	 * Download a file to the hotdir
    28	 * @param {string} url - The URL of the file to download
    29	 * @param {number} maxTimeout - The maximum timeout in milliseconds
    30	 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, fileLocation: string|null, reason: string|null}>} - The path to the downloaded file
    31	 */
    32	async function downloadURIToFile(url, maxTimeout = 10_000) {
    33	  if (!url || typeof url !== "string" || !validURL(url))
    34	    return { success: false, reason: "Not a valid URL.", fileLocation: null };
    35	
    36	  try {
    37	    const abortController = new AbortController();
    38	    const timeout = setTimeout(() => {
    39	      abortController.abort();
    40	      console.error(
    41	        `Timeout ${maxTimeout}ms reached while downloading file for URL:`,
    42	        url.toString()
    43	      );
    44	    }, maxTimeout);
    45	
    46	    const res = await fetch(url, { signal: abortController.signal })
    47	      .then((res) => {
    48	        if (!res.ok) throw new Error(`HTTP ${res.status}: ${res.statusText}`);
    49	        return res;
    50	      })
    51	      .finally(() => clearTimeout(timeout));
    52	
    53	    const urlObj = new URL(url);
    54	    let filename = `${urlObj.hostname}-${slugify(
    55	      urlObj.pathname.replace(/\//g, "-"),
    56	      { lower: true }
    57	    )}`;
    58	
    59	    // Check if the filename already has a valid extension that we support.
    60	    // If not, try to determine the extension from the Content-Type header.
    61	    const currentExt = path.extname(filename).toLowerCase();
    62	    const { SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS } = require("../constants");
    63	    if (!currentExt || !(currentExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
    64	      const contentType = res.headers.get("Content-Type");
    65	      const inferredExt = extensionFromContentType(contentType);
    66	      if (inferredExt) {
    67	        filename = filename + inferredExt;
    68	        console.log(
    69	          `[INFO]: Inferred file extension "${inferredExt}" from Content-Type "${contentType}" for URL: ${url}`
    70	        );
    71	      }
    72	    }
    73	
    74	    const localFilePath = path.join(WATCH_DIRECTORY, filename);
    75	    const writeStream = fs.createWriteStream(localFilePath);
    76	    await pipeline(res.body, writeStream);
    77	
    78	    console.log(`[SUCCESS]: File ${localFilePath} downloaded to hotdir.`);
    79	    return { success: true, fileLocation: localFilePath, reason: null };
    80	  } catch (error) {
    81	    console.error(`Error writing to hotdir: ${error} for URL: ${url}`);
    82	    return { success: false, reason: error.message, fileLocation: null };
    83	  }
    84	}
    85	
    86	module.exports = {
    87	  downloadURIToFile,
    88	};

Now I'm thinking about edge cases and potential improvements. Let me also consider the `processSingleFile` function. The `downloadURIToFile` fix handles the case when a URL is processed and the Content-Type is in `ACCEPTED_MIMES`. But what if:

1. The Content-Type is not in `ACCEPTED_MIMES` (e.g., `application/octet-stream`)?
2. The HEAD request fails but the GET request succeeds?

In these cases, `processSingleFile` would still fail. However, we could also improve `processSingleFile` to try to detect the file type from the file content (using the `isTextType` function or by reading magic bytes). But that's beyond the scope of the PR description.

Actually, let me reconsider. Let me look at the `processSingleFile` logic again:

```js
const fileExtension = path.extname(fullFilePath).toLowerCase();
if (fullFilePath.includes(".") && !fileExtension) {
    return {
      success: false,
      reason: `No file extension found. This file cannot be processed.`,
      documents: [],
    };
}

let processFileAs = fileExtension;
if (!SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS.hasOwnProperty(fileExtension)) {
    if (isTextType(fullFilePath)) {
      console.log(`...`);
      processFileAs = ".txt";
    } else {
      trashFile(fullFilePath);
      return {
        success: false,
        reason: `File extension ${fileExtension} not supported for parsing and cannot be assumed as text file type.`,
        documents: [],
      };
    }
}
```

The `isTextType` function uses `MimeDetector.getType` which uses the `mime` library. The `mime` library determines MIME type from file extension, not content. So for a file without a recognized extension, `mime.getType` returns null. Then `isKnownTextMime` returns `{ valid: false, reason: "generic" }`. Then `isTextType` falls back to `parseableAsText` which reads the first 1KB of the file and checks if it looks like text.

So for a PDF file without a `.pdf` extension:
- `mime.getType` returns null (unknown extension)
- `isKnownTextMime` returns `{ valid: false, reason: "generic" }` (since `mimeLib.badMimes` doesn't include null, and `mime.split("/")[0]` would throw because null can't be split)
- Wait, actually `mimeLib.getType` returns `null` if not found. Then `isKnownTextMime` does:
  ```js
  if (mimeLib.badMimes.includes(mime)) return { valid: false, reason: "bad_mime" };
  const type = mime.split("/")[0];
  ```
  If `mime` is null, `null.split("/")` would throw, so it goes to catch and returns `{ valid: false, reason: "generic" }`.
- Then `isTextType` calls `parseableAsText` which reads the first 1KB. A PDF file starts with `%PDF-1.x` which is text, so `parseableAsText` might return true! That means a PDF without extension would be processed as `.txt`, which is wrong.

But this is an edge case that existed before my change. My fix prevents this by ensuring the file gets a `.pdf` extension when the Content-Type indicates PDF.

Let me also think about another improvement: in `processSingleFile`, we could also check the file's MIME type from the `MimeDetector` and map it to a converter. But for now, the download fix should be sufficient.

Let me also double-check the `determineContentType` function to make sure the flow is correct:

1. `determineContentType(uri)` sends a HEAD request to get Content-Type
2. If Content-Type is in `ACCEPTED_MIMES` and not `text/html` or `text/plain`, `processVia = "file"`
3. `processAsFile` is called, which calls `downloadURIToFile(uri)` 
4. `downloadURIToFile` now properly appends extension from Content-Type
5. Then `processSingleFile` is called with the filename that now has the correct extension

This flow looks correct. But wait, there's also the case where `determineContentType` fails (e.g., HEAD request fails) - then `processVia` stays `"web"` and the URL is scraped as a webpage. That's fine.

Now let me also consider: should the `processAsFile` function also pass along the Content-Type information to `processSingleFile`? Currently it doesn't. But with my fix in `downloadURIToFile`, the extension is already corrected in the filename, so `processSingleFile` will work correctly.

However, there's one more scenario: what if `downloadURIToFile` is called from somewhere else (not through `processAsFile`)? Let me check if there are other callers:

Now let me think about edge cases more thoroughly:

1. **What if the filename already has a valid extension but the Content-Type indicates a different type?** 
   - Example: URL `https://example.com/file.pdf` with Content-Type `text/csv`
   - My code checks `if (!currentExt || !(currentExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS))` - since `.pdf` IS in `SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS`, it won't override. This is correct: we trust the explicit extension.

2. **What if the filename has no extension but Content-Type is also missing or not in ACCEPTED_MIMES?**
   - Example: URL `https://example.com/data` with Content-Type `application/octet-stream`
   - `extensionFromContentType` returns null, no extension is appended. The file goes to `processSingleFile` which will try `isTextType` and potentially fail. This is the same as before - no regression.

3. **What if the URL path has a query string?**
   - Example: `https://example.com/download?file=123`
   - `urlObj.pathname` is `/download`, so filename = `example.com-download`. Extension is empty. Content-Type should provide the extension.

4. **What about URLs with trailing dots or special characters?**
   - `slugify` handles special characters. The pathname replacement should handle most cases.

5. **What if there's already a file with the same name?**
   - This would be an issue before and after my change. The existing code doesn't handle duplicate filenames, but that's a separate concern.

I think my fix is solid. However, I want to also consider if there's a need to improve `processSingleFile` to handle the case where the extension is unknown but the file type could be detected from content. Let me look at this part again:

The PR description says the error originates from `processSingleFile/index.js#L58-L72`. The fix I made in `downloadURIToFile` addresses the root cause for URL downloads. But what about direct file uploads where the file has no extension? Should we also handle that?

Actually, let me re-read the PR description: "When attempting to pull and parse a file using either the RAG Modal or @agent mode, the process fails if the URL does not explicitly end with a file extension"

This is specifically about URLs. The fix in `downloadURIToFile` is the right place.

But wait, I should also consider: what if the `determineContentType` function (which uses a HEAD request) fails (e.g., server doesn't support HEAD), but the actual GET request in `downloadURIToFile` succeeds and returns a proper Content-Type? In that case, `processVia` would be `"web"` instead of `"file"`, and the URL would be scraped as a webpage instead of being downloaded as a file.

But that's a separate issue from the one described in the PR. The PR says the Content-Type header is present and correct.

Let me also check if there's a possibility that the `determineContentType` HEAD request succeeds but my `downloadURIToFile` GET request doesn't get the Content-Type header. That would be unusual - the Content-Type should be consistent between HEAD and GET.

I'm satisfied with the fix. Let me also consider if we should export the `extensionFromContentType` function in case other parts of the codebase need it. But for now, it's only used within `downloadURIToFile`.

Let me now run a more comprehensive test to simulate the actual flow:

cd /testbed/collector && cat > test_integration.js << 'EOF'
const path = require('path');
const { ACCEPTED_MIMES, SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS, WATCH_DIRECTORY } = require('./utils/constants');
const fs = require('fs');

// Simulate the new downloadURIToFile logic
function extensionFromContentType(contentType) {
  if (!contentType) return null;
  const mimeType = contentType.split(';')[0].trim().toLowerCase();
  if (mimeType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
    return ACCEPTED_MIMES[mimeType][0];
  }
  return null;
}

const { default: slugify } = require('slugify');

function simulateDownload(url, contentType) {
  const urlObj = new URL(url);
  let filename = urlObj.hostname + '-' + slugify(
    urlObj.pathname.replace(/\//g, '-'),
    { lower: true }
  );
  
  const currentExt = path.extname(filename).toLowerCase();
  if (!currentExt || !(currentExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
    const inferredExt = extensionFromContentType(contentType);
    if (inferredExt) {
      filename = filename + inferredExt;
    }
  }
  
  const finalExt = path.extname(filename).toLowerCase();
  const isSupported = finalExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS;
  
  return { filename, finalExt, isSupported };
}

// Test cases
const testCases = [
  {
    url: 'https://arxiv.org/pdf/2307.10265',
    contentType: 'application/pdf',
    description: 'Arxiv PDF without extension'
  },
  {

  },

  },

  },

    contentType: 'application/octet-stream',
    description: 'PDF extension but wrong content type (should trust extension)'
  },

console.log('Testing filename extension inference:\n');

let allPassed = true;
for (const test of testCases) {
  const result = simulateDownload(test.url, test.contentType);
  const status = result.isSupported ? '✓' : '✗';
  console.log(`${status} ${test.description}`);
  console.log(`  URL: ${test.url}`);
  console.log(`  Content-Type: ${test.contentType || 'none'}`);
  console.log(`  Filename: ${result.filename}`);
  console.log(`  Extension: ${result.finalExt}`);
  console.log(`  Supported: ${result.isSupported}`);
  console.log('');
  
  // Check that for known content types, the extension should be supported
  if (test.contentType && test.contentType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
    if (!result.isSupported) {
      console.log(`  ERROR: Expected supported extension for known content type!`);
      allPassed = false;
    }
  }
}

The `require("../constants")` is called at the top of the file already for `WATCH_DIRECTORY` and `ACCEPTED_MIMES`. I added a second require inside the function for `SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS`. It would be cleaner to just add `SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS` to the top-level require. Let me fix that:

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/collector/utils/downloadURIToFile/index.js   --old_str 'const { WATCH_DIRECTORY, ACCEPTED_MIMES } = require("../constants");
const fs = require("fs");
const path = require("path");
const { pipeline } = require("stream/promises");
const { validURL } = require("../url");
const { default: slugify } = require("slugify");

/**
 * Given a content-type header value, return the best matching file extension.
 * Uses the ACCEPTED_MIMES mapping to find the appropriate extension.
 * If no match is found, returns null.
 * @param {string} contentType - The Content-Type header value
 * @returns {string|null} - The file extension (including the dot) or null
 */
function extensionFromContentType(contentType) {
  if (!contentType) return null;
  // Only take the part before any semicolon (e.g., "application/pdf; charset=utf-8")
  const mimeType = contentType.split(";")[0].trim().toLowerCase();
  if (mimeType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
    // Return the first extension for this MIME type
    return ACCEPTED_MIMES[mimeType][0];
  }
  return null;
}

/**
 * Download a file to the hotdir
 * @param {string} url - The URL of the file to download
 * @param {number} maxTimeout - The maximum timeout in milliseconds
 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, fileLocation: string|null, reason: string|null}>} - The path to the downloaded file
 */
async function downloadURIToFile(url, maxTimeout = 10_000) {
  if (!url || typeof url !== "string" || !validURL(url))
    return { success: false, reason: "Not a valid URL.", fileLocation: null };

  try {
    const abortController = new AbortController();
    const timeout = setTimeout(() => {
      abortController.abort();
      console.error(
        `Timeout ${maxTimeout}ms reached while downloading file for URL:`,
        url.toString()
      );
    }, maxTimeout);

    const res = await fetch(url, { signal: abortController.signal })
      .then((res) => {
        if (!res.ok) throw new Error(`HTTP ${res.status}: ${res.statusText}`);
        return res;
      })
      .finally(() => clearTimeout(timeout));

    const urlObj = new URL(url);
    let filename = `${urlObj.hostname}-${slugify(
      urlObj.pathname.replace(/\//g, "-"),
      { lower: true }
    )}`;

    // Check if the filename already has a valid extension that we support.
    // If not, try to determine the extension from the Content-Type header.
    const currentExt = path.extname(filename).toLowerCase();
    const { SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS } = require("../constants");
    if (!currentExt || !(currentExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
      const contentType = res.headers.get("Content-Type");
      const inferredExt = extensionFromContentType(contentType);
      if (inferredExt) {
        filename = filename + inferredExt;
        console.log(
          `[INFO]: Inferred file extension "${inferredExt}" from Content-Type "${contentType}" for URL: ${url}`
        );
      }
    }

    const localFilePath = path.join(WATCH_DIRECTORY, filename);
    const writeStream = fs.createWriteStream(localFilePath);
    await pipeline(res.body, writeStream);

    console.log(`[SUCCESS]: File ${localFilePath} downloaded to hotdir.`);
    return { success: true, fileLocation: localFilePath, reason: null };
  } catch (error) {
    console.error(`Error writing to hotdir: ${error} for URL: ${url}`);
    return { success: false, reason: error.message, fileLocation: null };
  }
}' --new_str 'const {
  WATCH_DIRECTORY,
  ACCEPTED_MIMES,
  SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS,
} = require("../constants");
const fs = require("fs");
const path = require("path");
const { pipeline } = require("stream/promises");
const { validURL } = require("../url");
const { default: slugify } = require("slugify");

/**
 * Given a content-type header value, return the best matching file extension.
 * Uses the ACCEPTED_MIMES mapping to find the appropriate extension.
 * If no match is found, returns null.
 * @param {string} contentType - The Content-Type header value
 * @returns {string|null} - The file extension (including the dot) or null
 */
function extensionFromContentType(contentType) {
  if (!contentType) return null;
  // Only take the part before any semicolon (e.g., "application/pdf; charset=utf-8")
  const mimeType = contentType.split(";")[0].trim().toLowerCase();
  if (mimeType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
    // Return the first extension for this MIME type
    return ACCEPTED_MIMES[mimeType][0];
  }
  return null;
}

/**
 * Download a file to the hotdir
 * @param {string} url - The URL of the file to download
 * @param {number} maxTimeout - The maximum timeout in milliseconds
 * @returns {Promise<{success: boolean, fileLocation: string|null, reason: string|null}>} - The path to the downloaded file
 */
async function downloadURIToFile(url, maxTimeout = 10_000) {
  if (!url || typeof url !== "string" || !validURL(url))
    return { success: false, reason: "Not a valid URL.", fileLocation: null };

  try {
    const abortController = new AbortController();
    const timeout = setTimeout(() => {
      abortController.abort();
      console.error(
        `Timeout ${maxTimeout}ms reached while downloading file for URL:`,
        url.toString()
      );
    }, maxTimeout);

    const res = await fetch(url, { signal: abortController.signal })
      .then((res) => {
        if (!res.ok) throw new Error(`HTTP ${res.status}: ${res.statusText}`);
        return res;
      })
      .finally(() => clearTimeout(timeout));

    const urlObj = new URL(url);
    let filename = `${urlObj.hostname}-${slugify(
      urlObj.pathname.replace(/\//g, "-"),
      { lower: true }
    )}`;

    // Check if the filename already has a valid extension that we support.
    // If not, try to determine the extension from the Content-Type header.
    const currentExt = path.extname(filename).toLowerCase();
    if (!currentExt || !(currentExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
      const contentType = res.headers.get("Content-Type");
      const inferredExt = extensionFromContentType(contentType);
      if (inferredExt) {
        filename = filename + inferredExt;
        console.log(
          `[INFO]: Inferred file extension "${inferredExt}" from Content-Type "${contentType}" for URL: ${url}`
        );
      }
    }

    const localFilePath = path.join(WATCH_DIRECTORY, filename);
    const writeStream = fs.createWriteStream(localFilePath);
    await pipeline(res.body, writeStream);

    console.log(`[SUCCESS]: File ${localFilePath} downloaded to hotdir.`);
    return { success: true, fileLocation: localFilePath, reason: null };
  } catch (error) {
    console.error(`Error writing to hotdir: ${error} for URL: ${url}`);
    return { success: false, reason: error.message, fileLocation: null };
  }
}'

-const { WATCH_DIRECTORY } = require("../constants");
+const {
+  WATCH_DIRECTORY,
+  ACCEPTED_MIMES,
+  SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS,
+} = require("../constants");
 const fs = require("fs");
 const path = require("path");
 const { pipeline } = require("stream/promises");
 const { validURL } = require("../url");
 const { default: slugify } = require("slugify");
 
+/**
+ * Given a content-type header value, return the best matching file extension.
+ * Uses the ACCEPTED_MIMES mapping to find the appropriate extension.
+ * If no match is found, returns null.
+ * @param {string} contentType - The Content-Type header value
+ * @returns {string|null} - The file extension (including the dot) or null
+ */
+function extensionFromContentType(contentType) {
+  if (!contentType) return null;
+  // Only take the part before any semicolon (e.g., "application/pdf; charset=utf-8")
+  const mimeType = contentType.split(";")[0].trim().toLowerCase();
+  if (mimeType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
+    // Return the first extension for this MIME type
+    return ACCEPTED_MIMES[mimeType][0];
+  }
+  return null;
+}

  * @param {string} url - The URL of the file to download

     const urlObj = new URL(url);
-    const filename = `${urlObj.hostname}-${slugify(
+    let filename = `${urlObj.hostname}-${slugify(
       urlObj.pathname.replace(/\//g, "-"),
       { lower: true }
     )}`;
+
+    // Check if the filename already has a valid extension that we support.
+    // If not, try to determine the extension from the Content-Type header.
+    const currentExt = path.extname(filename).toLowerCase();
+    if (!currentExt || !(currentExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
+      const contentType = res.headers.get("Content-Type");
+      const inferredExt = extensionFromContentType(contentType);
+      if (inferredExt) {
+        filename = filename + inferredExt;
+        console.log(
+          `[INFO]: Inferred file extension "${inferredExt}" from Content-Type "${contentType}" for URL: ${url}`
+        );
+      }
+    }
+
     const localFilePath = path.join(WATCH_DIRECTORY, filename);
     const writeStream = fs.createWriteStream(localFilePath);
     await pipeline(res.body, writeStream);

+const {
+  WATCH_DIRECTORY,
+  ACCEPTED_MIMES,
+  SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS,
+} = require("../constants");
 const fs = require("fs");
 const path = require("path");
 const { pipeline } = require("stream/promises");
 const { validURL } = require("../url");
 const { default: slugify } = require("slugify");
 
+/**
+ * Given a content-type header value, return the best matching file extension.
+ * Uses the ACCEPTED_MIMES mapping to find the appropriate extension.
+ * If no match is found, returns null.
+ * @param {string} contentType - The Content-Type header value
+ * @returns {string|null} - The file extension (including the dot) or null
+ */
+function extensionFromContentType(contentType) {
+  if (!contentType) return null;
+  // Only take the part before any semicolon (e.g., "application/pdf; charset=utf-8")
+  const mimeType = contentType.split(";")[0].trim().toLowerCase();
+  if (mimeType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
+    // Return the first extension for this MIME type
+    return ACCEPTED_MIMES[mimeType][0];
+  }
+  return null;
+}

-const { WATCH_DIRECTORY } = require("../constants");
+const {
+  WATCH_DIRECTORY,
+  ACCEPTED_MIMES,
+  SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS,
+} = require("../constants");
 const fs = require("fs");
 const path = require("path");
 const { pipeline } = require("stream/promises");
 const { validURL } = require("../url");
 const { default: slugify } = require("slugify");
 
+/**
+ * Given a content-type header value, return the best matching file extension.
+ * Uses the ACCEPTED_MIMES mapping to find the appropriate extension.
+ * If no match is found, returns null.
+ * @param {string} contentType - The Content-Type header value
+ * @returns {string|null} - The file extension (including the dot) or null
+ */
+function extensionFromContentType(contentType) {
+  if (!contentType) return null;
+  // Only take the part before any semicolon (e.g., "application/pdf; charset=utf-8")
+  const mimeType = contentType.split(";")[0].trim().toLowerCase();
+  if (mimeType in ACCEPTED_MIMES) {
+    // Return the first extension for this MIME type
+    return ACCEPTED_MIMES[mimeType][0];
+  }
+  return null;
+}
+

+    if (!currentExt || !(currentExt in SUPPORTED_FILETYPE_CONVERTERS)) {
+      const contentType = res.headers.get("Content-Type");

+        filename = filename + inferredExt;
+        console.log(
+          `[INFO]: Inferred file extension "${inferredExt}" from Content-Type "${contentType}" for URL: ${url}`

+      }
+    }
